  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1b1fce3a-6b3f-44ff-b39b-15abb5542697'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9268495345470655595">Professor Theo Cray is trained to see patterns where others see chaos. So when mutilated bodies found deep in the Montana woods leave the cops searching blindly for clues, Theo sees something they missed. Something unnatural. Something only he can stop.<br/><br/>As a computational biologist, Theo is more familiar with digital code and microbes than the dark arts of forensic sleuthin</span>
  <span id="freeText9268495345470655595" style="display:none">Professor Theo Cray is trained to see patterns where others see chaos. So when mutilated bodies found deep in the Montana woods leave the cops searching blindly for clues, Theo sees something they missed. Something unnatural. Something only he can stop.<br /><br />As a computational biologist, Theo is more familiar with digital code and microbes than the dark arts of forensic sleuthing. But a field trip to Montana suddenly lands him in the middle of an investigation into the bloody killing of one of his former students. As more details, and bodies, come to light, the local cops determine that the killer is either a grizzly gone rogue… or Theo himself. Racing to stay one step ahead of the police, Theo must use his scientific acumen to uncover the killer. Will he be able to become as cunning as the predator he hunts—before he becomes its prey?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9268495345470655595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_41441250').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_41441250').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_41441250').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

<div id="review_2466452578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466452578" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2466452578?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2466452578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4133259580708858942">After my last, very meh, audiobook, I was happy to read The Naturalist. This one engaged me from the get go. Dr. Theo Cray is a computational biologist. To me, he seemed a little bit on the asperger’s spectrum. Extremely intelligent, definitely obsessive, but lacking a little in the emotive or self preservation factors. At one point he compares himself to Don Quixote and it’s a very apt description. They are both tilting at their own individual windmills. <br/><br/>He comes to the police’s attention after</span>
  <span id="freeText4133259580708858942" style="display:none">After my last, very meh, audiobook, I was happy to read The Naturalist. This one engaged me from the get go. Dr. Theo Cray is a computational biologist. To me, he seemed a little bit on the asperger’s spectrum. Extremely intelligent, definitely obsessive, but lacking a little in the emotive or self preservation factors. At one point he compares himself to Don Quixote and it’s a very apt description. They are both tilting at their own individual windmills. <br /><br />He comes to the police’s attention after the gruesome murder of a previous student of his. What are the odds of two scientists from Texas being in the same area of Montana doing research? But her death is ruled due to a grizzly bear mauling. Cray however, sees something else at play. <br /><br />I love that Mayne treats the reader’s intelligence with respect and gives us lots of science info. The book is almost stream of consciousness. We’re inside Theo’s head and a lot of interesting facts and theories reside there. Who knew that dolphins attack sharks when they’re incapacitated? There’s almost a contemplative feeling to the book as Theo spends a lot of time pondering what happened and how things connect. <br /><br />You’ll need to suspend your beliefs here. But it’s an interesting ride so I was willing to do so. <br /><br />I listened to this book and it works very well as an audiobook. I find a have a much more visceral reaction when listening to graphic scenes than when reading them. So there were lots of times I was twitching and flinching. <br /><br />There’s already a book two in this series out, which I’ll happily check out. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4133259580708858942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2115322490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2115322490" />
    <a title="Montzalee Wittmann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532051-montzalee-wittmann"><img alt="Montzalee Wittmann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538448191p2/32532051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2115322490?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Montzalee Wittmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Montzalee Wittmann" href="/user/show/32532051-montzalee-wittmann">Montzalee Wittmann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115322490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1968221210254353643">The Naturalist (The Naturalist #1) by Andrew Mayne is a book I really enjoyed. It fed my eager science side of my brain, the mystery, and the side that likes a good scare! Brilliantly written with so many little things that had to be thought through...wonderful. Going in my favorites for sure. Lots of suspense, action, mystery, and the science part of it was fun too. I love these kind of mysteries. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2331684859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2331684859" />
    <a title="Michael Hicks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6409681-michael-hicks"><img alt="Michael Hicks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498739220p2/6409681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2331684859?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Hicks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Hicks" href="/user/show/6409681-michael-hicks">Michael Hicks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6409681-michael-hicks?shelf=mystery-thriller-crime-suspense">mystery-thriller-crime-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6409681-michael-hicks?shelf=bought">bought</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2331684859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4821955290390635986">If Dan Brown wrote a CBS-style crime thriller, it'd probably look a lot like Andrew Mayne's <i>The Naturalist</i>. It's big dumb fun, quickly paced, and routinely threatened this reader's willing suspension of disbelief with a number of inanities, ridiculousness, and just flat-out stupid plot points. <i>The Naturalist</i> is a highly readable work of fluffy entertainment, one that is strangely compelling but also not very good.<br/><br/>Professor Theo Cray is a bioinformatics researcher, and when one of his former stud</span>
  <span id="freeText4821955290390635986" style="display:none">If Dan Brown wrote a CBS-style crime thriller, it'd probably look a lot like Andrew Mayne's <i>The Naturalist</i>. It's big dumb fun, quickly paced, and routinely threatened this reader's willing suspension of disbelief with a number of inanities, ridiculousness, and just flat-out stupid plot points. <i>The Naturalist</i> is a highly readable work of fluffy entertainment, one that is strangely compelling but also not very good.<br /><br />Professor Theo Cray is a bioinformatics researcher, and when one of his former students is found dead in the woods, he's the prime suspect until forensics lead authorities to believe she was mauled to death by a bear. Thanks to a case of mistaken identity, Cray is inadvertently given blood samples of the victim, which allows him to engage in some lone-hero forensic shenanigans that lead to the discovery that the bear hairs belong a tagged animal that died more than a year previously. Unable to let the case go, Cray uses his specialized knowledge in bioinformatics and learns of a number of missing women. Soon enough, he's on the trail of a serial killer who has somehow stayed off the grid for thirty years and may have killed hundreds and hundreds of women.<br /><br />If none of the above gives you pause, <i>The Naturalist</i> might be right up your alley. In order to discuss why <i>The Naturalist</i> didn't work for me, though, I need to point to some specifics, some truly bugfuck, batshit moments of high implausibility that really had me scratching my head. As such, I'm issuing a big <b>SPOILER WARNING from here on out. Consider yourself warned.</b><br /><br />Throughout <i>The Naturalist</i>, Mayne spares hardly a single thriller trope to get from point A to point B. We have the lone wolf hero who police refuse to even listen to, let alone believe, and who are perfectly content to ignore the discovery of all these butchered women. There's a hooker with a heart of gold, and the small ex-Army waitress hottie who, despite Cray's social ineptitude and naivete, still wants to bang our mousy, intrepid researcher. At some point in these types of thrillers it's a sure bet that our lone wolf hero will eventually be targeted by police as Prime Suspect #1. Well, Mayne begins the freaking book with that tired old trope, and then pulls it out of his butt a few more times throughout for good measure.<br /><br />Cray's doctorate and research has allowed him to learn a whole lot about a very small subject, leaving him oblivious to pretty much everything else. As he confesses a number of times, he doesn't know a lot about people. He can't read social cues, doesn't pick up on innuendo, and can't even decipher a text message from a hooker that reads "1004BJ". This cluelessness is, perhaps, meant to give Cray an easy pass by readers so that once he starts digging up dead bodies all across Montana and texting photos of the corpses to police, even going so far at one point as to load a murder victim into his SUV and dump the body off at the local police station, we're supposed to just accept this level of idiocy as par for the course. <br /><br />Unfortunately, I couldn't get over these hurdles, even as I watched with stony bemusement as Cray half-asses his way into stealing evidence, snatching a corpse from the morgue, and destroying crime scenes one right after another. And despite his reputation for these shenanigans eventually preceding him everywhere he goes, the police response is typically a bemusement equal to my own. After dumping a corpse off at the police station, Cray merely has to give a statement and is allowed on his merry way to go pilfer another body. <br /><br />The amount of WTFery is nested like Russian dolls throughout the entirety of <i>The Naturalist</i>, right down to its over-to-top, laugh out loud, implausible finale. Look, Cray is decidedly not a tough guy. He's a bookish nerd who gets beat up multiple times by various people, and Mayne still would have us believe that this guy is able to single-handedly take on an apex predator of a serial killer, a killer who has gone all <i>Terminator</i> in the book's final moments. Somehow, despite being shot three times and having previously been beaten unconscious and having his jaw fractured, Mayne still expects us to believe it's plausible that Cray would think, in all-caps, "I'M GOING TO TEAR THIS GUY APART!" and go all Wolverine beserker rage on a massive, bloodthirsty murderer. <br /><br />Did I mention I found this book utterly ridiculous? Because I did.<br /><br />That said, <i>The Naturalist</i> is stupidly entertaining but also perversely fascinating, and the scientific backbone Mayne weaves throughout is really interesting stuff. The research and thought processes that Cray brings to the table helps bring a measure of seriousness to an otherwise inanely written story, and Cray's eye for detail in the natural world is well done, lending a surprising amount of credibility to his field work. Unfortunately, when Cray isn't in the field and Mayne isn't focused on wowing us with science, the story takes some pretty steep nosedives.<br /><br />Readers expecting a serial killer thriller in the vein of <i>Silence of the Lambs</i> would do well to look elsewhere. If you don't mind a silly, check your brain at the door, beach read that's more comic book adventure than serious, well-studied suspense, you might do all right with this one if you keep expectations firmly in check. <i>The Naturalist</i> is ultimately pretty stupid, but at least it's entertainingly so. I didn't much care for it in the end, but I at least got my $3 worth of entertainment, and Mayne keeps the pacing cranked up to a high page-turning level. I found myself wanting to know how things were going to shake out, and morbidly curious as to just how much sillier it could get.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4821955290390635986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2143487807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143487807" />
    <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley"><img alt="Liz Barnsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447272680p2/16471876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143487807?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Barnsley" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley">Liz Barnsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143487807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer205070891852939565">Definitely the most addictive read of my year so far, borne out by the fact that I started this last night then finished it this morning - no messing. I literally only put it down to sleep.<br/><br/>For a start how wonderful to find something a bit different - I can't say I've read a book before where the main protagonist is a Computational Biologist - the author makes this sound entirely fascinating and if you have a love of finding out small random facts like I am you'll love the little titbits you find</span>
  <span id="freeText205070891852939565" style="display:none">Definitely the most addictive read of my year so far, borne out by the fact that I started this last night then finished it this morning - no messing. I literally only put it down to sleep.<br /><br />For a start how wonderful to find something a bit different - I can't say I've read a book before where the main protagonist is a Computational Biologist - the author makes this sound entirely fascinating and if you have a love of finding out small random facts like I am you'll love the little titbits you find throughout this novel. Not sure that Theo, our scientist, ever expected to use his expertise to track a serial killer nobody else will admit exists, but that is the situation he finds himself in after the death of a former student pulls him into an entirely different world.<br /><br />The Naturalist is a genuinely thrilling "serial killer thriller" with a scientific twist - the story fairly rocks along as Theo goes a bit lone wolf, albeit a rather less testosterone fueled one than you would normally find in this type of story, using his background and science geekery to seek out patterns and probabilities. That side of it is cleverly engaging, there is plenty of action besides and a hidden killer who will chill your soul. There are some intensely creepy moments in The Naturalist that made me jump at shadows a little and a real sense of menace all the way through. The ending is edge of the seat madness in the best way, a real blow out finale that rocked. From first page to last this was all the excellent, not a single boring moment. Brilliant.<br /><br />I see this listed as a book one - I have to say I'm extraordinarily pleased by the thought that Theo will be back. I loved him as an anchor to the rest of this tale, in fact all the characters within were brilliantly drawn and absolutely compelling, I hope to meet a few more of them again too.<br /><br />The Naturalist has excellent plotting, offers up a different perspective within the crime drama and who knows - perhaps Computational Biologists are the new Profilers - we'll see but on the basis of this book those writing within the crime genre might want to up their game. Seems there are ways to teach an old pony new tricks after all.<br /><br />Highly Recommended.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="205070891852939565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2206423639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2206423639" />
    <a title="Ann Marie (Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7447086-ann-marie-lit-wit-wine-dine"><img alt="Ann Marie (Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440945660p2/7447086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206423639?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann Marie (Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann Marie (Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine)" href="/user/show/7447086-ann-marie-lit-wit-wine-dine">Ann Marie (Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206423639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17119834645688850355">You can read this and all of my reviews at <a href='http://www.litwitwinedine.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine</a>.<br/><br/>Note: I originally posted that I was giving this book 3.5 stars. Upon further consideration, I've given it 3.75.<br/><br/>There are so many things I loved about <i>The Naturalis</i>t! First, there's our main man, Professor Theo Cray. He's a computational biologist. So basically he's a little nerdy, very smart, and, because he's now been drawn in to a murder investigation, a bit of a rogue Magnum, P.I. I'm not one for bookish crushes but if I were, he'd</span>
  <span id="freeText17119834645688850355" style="display:none">You can read this and all of my reviews at <a href="http://www.litwitwinedine.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Lit·Wit·Wine·Dine</a>.<br /><br />Note: I originally posted that I was giving this book 3.5 stars. Upon further consideration, I've given it 3.75.<br /><br />There are so many things I loved about <i>The Naturalis</i>t! First, there's our main man, Professor Theo Cray. He's a computational biologist. So basically he's a little nerdy, very smart, and, because he's now been drawn in to a murder investigation, a bit of a rogue Magnum, P.I. I'm not one for bookish crushes but if I were, he'd be a candidate.<br /><br />Next, there's the plot. What starts out as one dead woman, who happens to be a former student of Theo's, turns into multiple dead bodies. The crime scenes are gruesome. The victims appear to have been slashed to death by bear, mountain lion, or something else that's not quite human. The police are frustratingly unwilling to listen to Theo's opinions regarding who or what may have killed all of these women. This forces Theo to strike out on his on own quest for the killer. His scientific knowledge lends an element that I've rarely read in this genre. He uses biology, anthropology, botany, statistics, and computer algorithms together in order to locate the bodies and predict where more may be located.<br /><br />As far as pacing goes, I found <i>The Naturalist</i> to be an absolute page-turner. I read it in one day. I loved that the chapters are short and the action moves along steadily.<br /><br />I did have a couple of small issues with the book. The first is relatively minor. I found Theo's grief over the former student who had been killed to be greater than I would have expected. That may seem insensitive but they'd only had a professional relationship and they hadn't spoken in years. The second - and you know I'm a stickler for this - is plausibility. Particularly as it relates to the ending. I won't give it away because it was quite imaginative but, as a nurse, I must admit I rolled my eyes more than once. I actually think the final scene would translate very well in film but it just seemed a bit too much as I read it on the pages. In my opinion, this is a classic case of an author's brilliant imagination being both a blessing and a curse. Had the ending been dialed back a bit, I'm sure I could have given this book four to four and a half stars.<br /><br />This is the first book in <i>The Naturalist<i> series. I am very much looking forward to reading the next book.<br /><br />3.75/5 glasses of wine<br /><br />Many thanks to Thomas &amp; Mercer for providing me with a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /></i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17119834645688850355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2443308285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2443308285" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2443308285?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=nature-themes">nature-themes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443308285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5569885346848697746">"What is research but a blind date with knowledge." (William Henry)<br/><br/>And Professor Theo Cray of the University of Texas at Austin knows research up close and personal. He's an MIT graduate specializing in computational biology. Analyzing data and constructing models brings Theo eye to eye with biological, behavioral, and social systems. Funny how such lofty studies might shine a light on a recent dead body.<br/><br/>Andrew Mayne starts his story out with a bang. Theo Cray's motel room in a small town in Mon</span>
  <span id="freeText5569885346848697746" style="display:none">"What is research but a blind date with knowledge." (William Henry)<br /><br />And Professor Theo Cray of the University of Texas at Austin knows research up close and personal. He's an MIT graduate specializing in computational biology. Analyzing data and constructing models brings Theo eye to eye with biological, behavioral, and social systems. Funny how such lofty studies might shine a light on a recent dead body.<br /><br />Andrew Mayne starts his story out with a bang. Theo Cray's motel room in a small town in Montana is under fire by the local police. Cray is roughly tossed to the ground and handcuffed with no clue as to why. An empty ice bucket lays on the ground next to him as the only reminder of what "normal" was in the past tense. Here on out, chaos and mayhem will rule the days and the nights.<br /><br />Theo is finally told that a former student of his at UTA was found dead in the forest not too far from where the motel sits. His Texas plates are a dead giveaway in the parking lot. Through hours of interrogation, Theo is finally allowed to leave. As the days go by, it is believed that Juniper was killed by a grizzly. A grizzly is taken down by a local hunter nearby with a single shot. End of story you say. Not so fast.....<br /><br />It's this hyper analytical nature that spins the wheels at a roaring pace within the mind of Theo Cray. Hell bent on finding out what really happened to Juniper, Theo visits the scene and is convinced that Juniper's demise was due to the two-legged variety. But convincing the local police is like dragging thousand pound stones up the sides of the pyramids. An impossible task, but one in which Theo is willing to take on.<br /><br />As Theo implements computer analysis and his hardcore familiarity of botany and ecosystems, he begins to unveil some crazy off-the-wall theories. We could be in for more dead bodies and a possible serial killer here, Boys and Girls. WooHoo!<br /><br />Mayne brings in plenty of science around the campfire in The Naturalist. He does it in such a way that the reader is not overwhelmed, but pleasantly piques interest. In order to totally enjoy this wild ride, just sit back and let this story unfold. There may be a few camels slipping through the eye of the needle here and there, but it's full-on entertainment. The ending is chock full of adrenaline pumping action in which an adult beverage may be warranted. Good stuff.<br /><br />The Naturalist is the first book in this series. I've already grabbed the next one. A well thought out storyline with high interest. Let's see what double trouble Andrew Mayne will drop Theo into down this curving road. Binoculars optional.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5569885346848697746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2115322385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2115322385" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2115322385?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=arcs-and-galleys">arcs-and-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115322385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2129067666455379862">4.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://bibliosanctum.com/2017/10/23/book-review-the-naturalist-by-andrew-mayne/'>https://bibliosanctum.com/2017/10/23/...</a><br/><br/>I spent a day last week stumbling around in a sleep-deprived stupor because I had been up late the night before, and it was all this book’s fault since I’d refused to put it down until I was finished. Totally worth it, though. Talk about a page-turner! The Naturalist was exactly what I wanted out of a mystery-thriller—fascinating, addictive, and dramatic in all the best ways. It also captivated the science geek in me by </span>
  <span id="freeText2129067666455379862" style="display:none">4.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bibliosanctum.com/2017/10/23/book-review-the-naturalist-by-andrew-mayne/">https://bibliosanctum.com/2017/10/23/...</a><br /><br />I spent a day last week stumbling around in a sleep-deprived stupor because I had been up late the night before, and it was all this book’s fault since I’d refused to put it down until I was finished. Totally worth it, though. Talk about a page-turner! The Naturalist was exactly what I wanted out of a mystery-thriller—fascinating, addictive, and dramatic in all the best ways. It also captivated the science geek in me by featuring a protagonist who uses the study of plant and animal behavior and physiology to solve crimes, his specialized knowledge allowing him to spot patterns where others cannot. Think The Da Vinci Code, but with biology.<br /><br />Our story begins as computational biologist Theo Cray gets a call from the police while on a field research trip in Montana. The body of Juniper Parsons, one of his ex-students, has been found in the woods near a small town, and the cause of death appears to have been a rogue grizzly attack. However, Theo is not convinced, recognizing unnatural signs in the evidence. Despite the terrible claw marks and the traces of fur on the victim, he’s not sure that whatever killed her was even an animal. More likely it was a man, he insists. Killing like an animal.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the police are no help, especially once Fish and Wildlife Service puts down the bear believed to be responsible for the savage attack. Knowing that his former student’s true killer is still out there though, Theo is unwilling to give up and decides to conduct his own investigation, uncovering a disturbing pattern of missing persons reports and mysterious deaths that go back for more than thirty years. All the incidents happened in or around the state of Montana, many of them involving young women. In the cases where remains were recovered, the mutilated bodies all displayed the same kind of claw marks found on Juniper Parsons. Following a trail of clues, Theo begins finding more victims and knows he’s getting closer to the truth, though inevitably his efforts draw unwanted attention as the police start suspecting Theo himself.<br /><br />The Naturalist is the perfect thriller novel for the science lover. Yes, it can get a little farfetched at times, requiring the reader to simply roll with it, but with a story this enthralling and irresistible, you’d be surprised at how much I’m willing to let slide. A couple of minor plot holes and a few dubious moments were not enough to detract from the enjoyment.<br /><br />Another amazing thing about this book is its protagonist. Theo is a professor in an extremely esoteric field, so he’s always having a hard time getting others to understand his evidence or how he’s getting his data. It also doesn’t help that he’s a bit socially awkward, and his brain is wired to think in a very different way than most people. In spite of this though, I found him remarkably easy to relate to—and not just because of the shared interest in biological sciences. Above all, Theo is driven by a sense of duty towards his murdered student, and while his guilt and emotional self-punishment may have been a tad unfounded, it’s hard not to feel sympathetic towards someone whose heart is so genuine and in the right place. He attacks his mission with indefatigable zeal that almost borders on obsession, but you’ve also got to admire his persistence, especially when he finds ways to get creative. While Theo is highly intelligent, his doggedness and complete lack of street smarts often leads to solutions with successful results but appalling side effects.<br /><br />Then there’s the plot, which sank its hooks into me and dug in deep. The story’s tone and style are arguably similar to that of most thrillers, but like I said, this novel had a scientific angle to it that made it special. A good balance of action and suspense kept the pace swift and strong, and some of the more mysterious and atmospheric scenes were even touched with a hint of horror. The final chapters of the book, AKA the section that had me devouring the pages at the expense of a good night’s sleep, were so intense and insane that I doubt I could have stopped reading even if the house was burning down around me.<br /><br />Man, I really hope I won’t have long to wait for the sequel, because it does appear The Naturalist is the first book of a new series. Cleverly addictive and hugely entertaining, this book had me hanging on every word from start to finish. If I’m reading a lot more mystery-thriller these days, well, it’s because of books like this, and I can’t wait to read more from Andrew Mayne.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2129067666455379862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2286855826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2286855826" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36199787-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445213837p2/36199787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2286855826?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/36199787-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36199787-jim?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36199787-jim?shelf=books-read-2020">books-read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2286855826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5695092082086347475">This was the first book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/378554.Andrew_Mayne' title='Andrew Mayne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Andrew Mayne</a> that I have read. It probably won't be my last but I am not in any big hurry to read another one. It was entertaining and if you like the mystery / suspense / thriller genre you probably would enjoy this one but it wasn't anything that grabbed me.<br/><br/>Professor Theo Cray is a computational biologist who is in Montana on a grant doing a study on something. Frogs? Whatever. The story opens with him heading to the ice machine at the motel where he staying when the</span>
  <span id="freeText5695092082086347475" style="display:none">This was the first book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/378554.Andrew_Mayne" title="Andrew Mayne" rel="nofollow noopener">Andrew Mayne</a> that I have read. It probably won't be my last but I am not in any big hurry to read another one. It was entertaining and if you like the mystery / suspense / thriller genre you probably would enjoy this one but it wasn't anything that grabbed me.<br /><br />Professor Theo Cray is a computational biologist who is in Montana on a grant doing a study on something. Frogs? Whatever. The story opens with him heading to the ice machine at the motel where he staying when the police swoop in and bust down the door of one of the rooms. His room. He is apparently a person of interest in the death of a former student who happened to be in the area. He is taken to the police headquarters where he is questioned. At some point it is determined that the former student was killed by a bear. You can go now Theo. Sorry for the inconvenience. I have never been in this situation but I think most people would breath a sigh of relief and just go. Back to Texas (Theo is a professor at the University of Texas at Austin). Anywhere but Montana.<br /><br />Theo is not satisfied and decides to investigate further. He singly handed starts finding bodies. All apparently classified as bear or mountain lion attacks. Analyzing the data and using computer models he detects a pattern and determines these are the work of a serial killer who has gone undetected. In the process Theo keeps bringing attention to himself to various law enforcement agencies in Montana. They alternately consider him a suspect in the deaths or someone with mental issues. With the help of a waitress at a local diner he decides to find out who the serial killer is. School and the start of classes can wait.<br /><br />This was an entertaining story if you are willing to go along with the ride and suspend belief. I actually found myself liking Theo and cheering him on in his Don Quixote quest. I would be willing to read other books in the series at some point if only to see what the future holds for Theo. It is hard to imaging that he will still be a professor the University of Texas at Austin after this.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5695092082086347475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2440787283" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2440787283" />
    <a title="Fred Shaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44212467-fred-shaw"><img alt="Fred Shaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545362118p2/44212467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2440787283?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fred Shaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fred Shaw" href="/user/show/44212467-fred-shaw">Fred Shaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2440787283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14268184859949776476">The Naturalist by Andrew Mayne, Kindle edition. <br/><br/>Dr. Theo Cray is a professor of biogenics and uses computer models to determine how biological systems react given certain criteria. In Montana, while conducting a study, he learns that a previous student was just killed by a grisly bear. To most of the law enforcement, that is what it appears to have happened, but Dr. Cray was not convinced. However, the police and department of natural resources had their collective minds made up, so they track a</span>
  <span id="freeText14268184859949776476" style="display:none">The Naturalist by Andrew Mayne, Kindle edition. <br /><br />Dr. Theo Cray is a professor of biogenics and uses computer models to determine how biological systems react given certain criteria. In Montana, while conducting a study, he learns that a previous student was just killed by a grisly bear. To most of the law enforcement, that is what it appears to have happened, but Dr. Cray was not convinced. However, the police and department of natural resources had their collective minds made up, so they track a likely bear suspect and terminate it. <br /><br />After reviewing missing persons accounts in the area over a period of years, he finds that most of the subjects were young women, and believes there might be more similarities in their disappearance to his friend’s death. If the women did not get lost in the Montana mountains but were in fact murdered, and no bodies found, could there be a serial killer effectively hiding the evidence so well that he/she could get away with over a 30 year period?<br /><br />The story is entertaining, but so much of the the protagonist’s activity is repetitive making the read tedious. Secondly, the good professor is almost too good to be true, having such a vast knowledge of the environment that he outsmarts all law enforcement and locals and goes after the killer single handedly. This is the first in a series and I am debating whether to read the next in line.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14268184859949776476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2203602885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203602885" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597768154p2/67496521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2203602885?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=science">science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203602885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17529846469167035313">3.5/5 stars<br/><br/>If you enjoy the tv channel <i>Investigation Discovery</i> or shows like <i>Forensic Files</i>, then Andrew Mayne's <b>
  <i>The Naturalist</i>
</b> is the perfect read for you! It is a quick, dark read that doesn't sugar coat the plot, while not explicitly getting too grotesque. The story starts off with Dr. Theo Cray being questioned about the disappearance of one of his past students, Juniper, who police claim has a direct link to Dr. Cray. After routine questioning, police confirm Juniper's death as an accid</span>
  <span id="freeText17529846469167035313" style="display:none">3.5/5 stars<br /><br />If you enjoy the tv channel <i>Investigation Discovery</i> or shows like <i>Forensic Files</i>, then Andrew Mayne's <b>
  <i>The Naturalist</i>
</b> is the perfect read for you! It is a quick, dark read that doesn't sugar coat the plot, while not explicitly getting too grotesque. The story starts off with Dr. Theo Cray being questioned about the disappearance of one of his past students, Juniper, who police claim has a direct link to Dr. Cray. After routine questioning, police confirm Juniper's death as an accidental bear attack in the nearby woods. Dr. Cray, professor and biologist, can't leave well enough alone because if Juniper was a dedicated student of his, she would know how to react to a bear in the woods. As Dr. Cray investigates the small Montana town that he's visiting, he begins to see how a town crippled by drugs, poverty, and a lack of education can only continue on by keeping their darkest secrets hidden. Through Dr. Cray's investigation, he realizes that things aren't always what it may seem.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Naturalist</i>
</b> was very different read for me—it had a lot of science background in it that I was not familiar (nor really wanted to be familiar) with, while keeping me on the edge of my seat by keeping the mystery at bay. Dr. Cray was sarcastic, witty, and a profound protagonist for me. This book is approximately 400 pages, but the dialogue isn't overtly sophisticated so you can easily brush through this read quickly. <b>
  <i>The Naturalist</i>
</b>'s storyline was very original in a sense that it took key common themes (i.e.: drugs, town corruption, crime), and interweaving it into a robust plot development. I would also recommend anyone who enjoys anything by David Bell or Noah Hawley to definitely pick this one up. I immediately got <i>Bring Her Home</i> and <i>Before The Fall</i> vibes as I was trekking on with the story although neither book is similar in terms of content. <br /><br />This book will not be for everyone—I'm telling you now. If you really aren't into the multifaceted world of biology, genetics, DNA, etc; this isn't the read for you. At points <b>
  <i>The Naturalist</i>
</b> can be a little <i>too</i> technical and I had to catch myself from skipping through those sections. Once I was about 1/3 of the way into the story, I actually began to care more about the characters and was focused on finishing. <br /><br /><b>I was provided a copy of <i>The Naturalist</i> in exchange for an honest review. Thank you Wunderbooks PR, it was a pleasure.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17529846469167035313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2147769663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147769663" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27125460-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527772449p2/27125460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147769663?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/27125460-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147769663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12295742174589999643">It took me forever to read this book because #1. I kept falling asleep and #2. I dreaded picking it back up. Generally speaking, the story line was stupid, the characters were shallow and poorly developed, the action scenes were overly complicated and hard to envision, and the main character was so boring, I don't even remember his name. The first 30% of the book was like reading an encyclopedic entry on bears. Was the author trying to make us think a bear really was the killer? Or was he just s</span>
  <span id="freeText12295742174589999643" style="display:none">It took me forever to read this book because #1. I kept falling asleep and #2. I dreaded picking it back up. Generally speaking, the story line was stupid, the characters were shallow and poorly developed, the action scenes were overly complicated and hard to envision, and the main character was so boring, I don't even remember his name. The first 30% of the book was like reading an encyclopedic entry on bears. Was the author trying to make us think a bear really was the killer? Or was he just showing off all the research he did on bears? Either way, it was obvious in the first chapter that the killer was not a bear, so why spend all that time boring me with details about bears? Eventually, the main character turns into this pompous know-it-all, who is doing the police's job because the police are inept. It irritated me that he was supposed to be so smart, yet he didn't see that he was making himself look like the killer. Well, not until the end when the light bulb finally went off. Queue the requisite "love interest". Could two characters have any less chemistry? And the "big sex scene" is in a car on the side of a road after they found ANOTHER dead body and are being followed? I need more synonyms for the words stupid and dumb. The book was peppered with scenes and set ups that had nothing to do with the story, only to provide a solution on the following page. The main character (still can't remember his stupid name), would go into great detail explaining the most obvious simple thought process. Not everything needs to be explained. Readers are smart enough to connect the dots. But perhaps the most insulting feature was his uncanny ability to make an assumption and have it lead perfectly to the next victim or even more unbelievably, the perfect clue. I didn't want to waste my time finishing this book, but I wanted to give it a review worthy of it's horribleness, so I forced myself to finish so I could offer this review. I notice that this book is the first in a series, I seriously have doubts about the person who signed that deal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12295742174589999643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369438833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7662590285991358966">What a wild ride! In this mystery-suspense-thriller, the story opens with Professor Theo Cray, a computational biologist, being questioned about a possible murder of a former student. He is released when police determine that a bear or mountain lion was involved. Or was it? <br/><br/>Professor Theo Cray is a remarkable character. He’s a brilliant scientist, and his strengths lie in numbers, systems, patterns, data-modeling, and methodical analysis. He is socially awkward when dealing with people. I found </span>
  <span id="freeText7662590285991358966" style="display:none">What a wild ride! In this mystery-suspense-thriller, the story opens with Professor Theo Cray, a computational biologist, being questioned about a possible murder of a former student. He is released when police determine that a bear or mountain lion was involved. Or was it? <br /><br />Professor Theo Cray is a remarkable character. He’s a brilliant scientist, and his strengths lie in numbers, systems, patterns, data-modeling, and methodical analysis. He is socially awkward when dealing with people. I found it clever and riveting, the very definition of a page-turner. I can’t vouch for the accuracy of the police procedures, medicine, or forensics, but I have a feeling some of it was over the top. I chose to suspend disbelief and found myself thoroughly entertained. <br /><br />I don’t often read series, but I just may have to pick up the sequel to see what Professor Cray gets up to next. Content includes profanity, violence, and gruesome descriptions of mutilated bodies. Recommended to readers that enjoy mystery-thrillers with a side of science.</span>

<div id="review_2115986248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2115986248" />
    <a title="JustSomeGuy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36920718-justsomeguy"><img alt="JustSomeGuy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461698476p2/36920718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2115986248?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JustSomeGuy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JustSomeGuy" href="/user/show/36920718-justsomeguy">JustSomeGuy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115986248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14878208847503890937">Deciding to read this one was a total shot in the dark as I was without a book waiting for the library to re-open after the holiday break with books I had on hold. My September First Read email from Amazon came and I immediately selected this based on the primer sentence alone. Past selections of the First Read benefit have not gone well, but this one started out as a surprising exception. The main character in this book is the total opposite of a traditional protagonist - he's a socially awkwar</span>
  <span id="freeText14878208847503890937" style="display:none">Deciding to read this one was a total shot in the dark as I was without a book waiting for the library to re-open after the holiday break with books I had on hold. My September First Read email from Amazon came and I immediately selected this based on the primer sentence alone. Past selections of the First Read benefit have not gone well, but this one started out as a surprising exception. The main character in this book is the total opposite of a traditional protagonist - he's a socially awkward wuss brainiac who stumbles into a crime initially thought to be a bear attack. I bought into the scientific approach used by Professor Theo Cray as a replacement for formal sleuthing and enjoyed his total lack of physical presence and near complete inability to relate to people. The author does a great job describing how Cray's anti-social behavior isn't just a challenge for him personally, but how he's also viewed by others - including the police. Unfortunately, the book doesn't do much to foster the question readers could have started to ask: is he the psychopath killer or just an awkward amateur investigator professor genius? How accurate is the science? I don't know, but I bought into it enough to plow through the first half of the book. Unfortunately, things began falling apart for me once Cray starting to get a beat on the killer - readily using his repurposed computer model to figure out a pattern to locate the killers victims and even where his killing days began. By the time we race towards a ludicrous finale where the total wuss nerd takes on a jacked up, armored killing machine, the book lost a lot of the equity it had built up with me to that point. I was ready to add this series and Mayne to my To Read list, but I'm left torn between the promise of how this one started out and the steep decline the story took toward a ridiculous ending. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14878208847503890937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2268103220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268103220" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4440925-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562019138p2/4440925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268103220?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/4440925-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4440925-debbie?shelf=top-reads">top-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4440925-debbie?shelf=authors-i-love">authors-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4440925-debbie?shelf=serial-killer">serial-killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4440925-debbie?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268103220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5562413144826655929">Wow!!! I haven't had that much fun reading a book in a long, long time! Don't get me wrong this serial killer thriller....thrills. It has it's seriously creepy, tense and edge of your seat moments but it was also extremely fun to read (yeah, I'm a little wacked), perfectly paced and balanced. <br/><br/>This book follows Theo, the quintessential, socially awkward, and common sense lacking scientist, as he gets caught up in the hunt for the serial killer responsible for the death of his former student. And </span>
  <span id="freeText5562413144826655929" style="display:none">Wow!!! I haven't had that much fun reading a book in a long, long time! Don't get me wrong this serial killer thriller....thrills. It has it's seriously creepy, tense and edge of your seat moments but it was also extremely fun to read (yeah, I'm a little wacked), perfectly paced and balanced. <br /><br />This book follows Theo, the quintessential, socially awkward, and common sense lacking scientist, as he gets caught up in the hunt for the serial killer responsible for the death of his former student. And when I say caught up, I really mean he is the only one hunting. Law enforcement cannot see what is so blatantly obvious to Theo. His scientific mind demands the answers and the man within can't walk away. To my surprise, I was completely endeared with Theo. His mind was completely beyond my comprehension but the man well, he brought out the fixer in me. I wanted to be his life coach, instill some much needed guidance and maybe a slap or two upside the head. ;)<br /><br />I'll be honest, I didn't always understand the science but the cool thing is I didn't have to to enjoy the story. Plus, I managed to learn a thing or two. This story, I imagine, pushes science to its edge and maybe over it some too and there are scenes that are over the top a smidgen. But isn't that what a good story teller does? They take the believable and give it and edge, embellish the truth, intensify the climax, and in the end, the story is better and more enjoyable for everyone. If you're science minded and are going to split hairs over every theory, walk away but if you want to enjoy and excellently written story with one of the best endings ever, read on!<br /><br />This is my first book by Andrew Mayne but I am chomping at the bit to move on to the next one. Angel Killer here I come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5562413144826655929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2858639735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2858639735" />
    <a title="Pat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407123-pat"><img alt="Pat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591983365p2/7407123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2858639735?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pat" href="/user/show/7407123-pat">Pat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2858639735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1333120284714881353">My quest for 'something a bit different' in reading material has borne much fruit lately. Meet Dr Theo Cray, one of the most unusual protagonists in a crime thriller you will ever meet. He is a very geeky computational biologist. He searches for patterns in nature and has written an advanced computer program to analyse these.<br/><br/>So there he is in Montana doing some field research when he is abruptly bundled off to a police station for questioning about the death of one of his former students. It's n</span>
  <span id="freeText1333120284714881353" style="display:none">My quest for 'something a bit different' in reading material has borne much fruit lately. Meet Dr Theo Cray, one of the most unusual protagonists in a crime thriller you will ever meet. He is a very geeky computational biologist. He searches for patterns in nature and has written an advanced computer program to analyse these.<br /><br />So there he is in Montana doing some field research when he is abruptly bundled off to a police station for questioning about the death of one of his former students. It's not long before he is cleared and the killing attributed to a bear attack but Theo's interest is piqued (he's geeky alright but has an insatiable curiosity about things). He checks out the crime scene and goes into the data base (apparently there is one for research purposes) of known bears in the region. He soon picks up an anomaly that means a bear couldn't have done it, therefore it must have been a man (or woman) trying to make it look like a bear attack. He takes this info to the authorities but of course, as it questions their credibility, his theory is about as welcome as a fart in a lift (elevator for you Americans). Undaunted, Theo can't seem to let it go. Maybe the killer has struck before because surely a first time killer would not have done this, nor be prepared with a bear hair which screams "premeditation" to place at the scene.<br /><br />He uses his computer models and analytical skills to develop hypotheses and races off to investigate on his own. Despite a few hiccups he finds another victim in a shallow grave with all the hallmarks of a bear attack. More analysis, more skepticism by the authorities but he perseveres and is soon digging up bodies left, right and centre. Well knock me over with a feather, this eventually brings him to the attention of the killer and Theo has no idea what he is in for. <br /><br />What an interesting book! Chock full of interesting scientific facts processes that are simply explained and gripping at the same time. Theo was kind of endearing in a geeky and socially inept way. The ending was highly suspenseful and stretched credulity a bit. Nevertheless a thoroughly different and entertaining story. I've already bought book two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1333120284714881353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2259609131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2259609131" />
    <a title="Rade " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8187431-rade"><img alt="Rade " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2259609131?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rade " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rade " href="/user/show/8187431-rade">Rade </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2259609131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2609270588111868903">This book is one of the best reasons why I shouldn't rely on others to tell me what needs to be read because "you will not be able to put it down. It is that good". <br/><br/>Well, I hate to disappoint but I did put this book down, a lot. So much so that I at times read five pages and got up to do something else, not going back to the book for days. <br/><br/>In its core, I don't think the book was that bad. However, there a lot of plot holes in this book that I couldn't get over. From one of the characters (not me</span>
  <span id="freeText2609270588111868903" style="display:none">This book is one of the best reasons why I shouldn't rely on others to tell me what needs to be read because "you will not be able to put it down. It is that good". <br /><br />Well, I hate to disappoint but I did put this book down, a lot. So much so that I at times read five pages and got up to do something else, not going back to the book for days. <br /><br />In its core, I don't think the book was that bad. However, there a lot of plot holes in this book that I couldn't get over. From one of the characters (not mentioning who) being a goddamn Superman by the end of the book to a mapping system almost never being wrong and always leading characters where they need to go, the book was filled with too many coincidences. Everything seems to fit in to what the characters were doing. They look for clues in one spot and it leads them to a gigantic discovery that even the best of professionals never bothered to check, apparently. <br /><br />I don't remember any of the characters either. They are forgettable, thrown here and there to keep the plot moving with no "meat" to them. They were a little too one dimensional for my liking and didn't bring much to the conversation. Half of them didn't believe the main character, and despite probably getting a lot of evidence on him, the main character suffered rather mild slap on the wrist for his action, especially for the dead body segment close to the end. <br /><br />Also, whatever happened to his job? Did he get fired? <br /><br />Anyway, I am over the book. I am moving on from this character who is not only knowledgeable in just about everything the situation demands, but can also think on his feet no matter how cornered he is. Where is the vulnerability? If he got none, I ain't relating to him. <br /><br />That is all. <br /><br />R.S<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2609270588111868903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SaQSbFE5wzJ80BIt26Czh/w2SCbzSvoDZQ13Cb/SGs/vXyuEuWODivhFirLF6qZ93JQgOYGKsFXDr/Cb/lATnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XXr95rwA2nbjS5oiWrYXi9Ql12unfZm4ljdgYgXJRhX7gcQOVFqazmfeAr1E/AJx9Ie/dNW90+4wlefwREtPRw==')})
  }
